كتاب الشهادة كالبيع والإقرار وحكم الحاكم والغصب والقتل وإن لم يشهد عليه ولا يشهد على شهادة غيره ما لم يشهد عليه، ولا يعمل شاهد الموجب بنفسه، وهو الشرط؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَنْ شَهِدَ بِالْحَقِّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ (الزخرف:٨٦)، والأولى أن يقول: أشهد أنه باع أو أقر أو حكم أو غصب أو قتل؛ لأنه عاين بالسبب، فوجب عليه الشهادة به، ولا يقول: أشهدني إلا إذا أشهده كي لا يكون كاذباً، ولو سمع من وراء الحجاب إقرار شخص، لا يسعه أن يشهد؛ لاحتمال أن يكون غيره ؛ إذ النغمة تشبه النغمة إلا إذا دخل البيت وعلم أنه ليس فيه غيره. ثم خرج وقعد على الباب، وليس للبيت مدخل غيره، فسمع إقرار من في البيت ولا يراه، فحينئذ حل له أن يشهد على إقراره وينبغي للقاضي إذا فسر له بأن قال أشهد بالسماع من وراء الحجاب، أن يقبل الشهادة، ألا ترى أن الشهادة بالتسامع إنما يجوز في الأشياء الستة، كما سيجيء في المتن، وقالوا: إذا سمع صوت امرأة من وراء الحجاب لا يجوز أن يشهد عليها، إلا إذا كان يرى شخصها، ونوع لا يثبت حكمه بنفسه كالشهادة على الشهادة، فإذا سمع يشهد بشيء، لم يجز للسامع أن يشهد على شهادته إلا يشهده، وأشار إلى هذا بقوله: ولا يشهد على شهادة غيره إلخ. (عيني، فتح، عناية) شاهداً وإن لم يشهد أي وإن لم يشهده أحد من أصحاب تلك العقود والحقوق والحاكم. (عيني) عليه: أي على ما صدر من القول والفعل. (عيني ولا يشهد على شهادة إلخ لأن الشهادة ليست موجبة بنفسها، وإنما تصير موجبة بعد النقل إلى مجلس القضاء، فيشترط فيها النيابة والتحمل، ولم يوجد فلا يجوز، وكذا إذا سمعه يشهد غيره على شهادته، لا يسعه أن يشهد؛ لأنه لم يحمله وإنما حمل غيره رمز الحقائق: ١٤٢/٢] فصار نظير ما لو شخصا يوكل حيث لا يجوز للسامع أن يتصرف ما لم يوكله؛ لأن الموكل لم يرض برأيه، ولابد من قبول التحمل وعدم النهي بعده ، وقيد بالشهادة على الشهادة؛ لأن الشهادة بقضاء القاضي صحيحة وإن لم يشهده القاضي عليه؛ لأن القضاء حجة ملزمة فحل له أن يشهد بها. (عيني، فتح) سمع ما لم يشهد : أي ما لم يقل له الشاهد: اشهد على شهادتي. (عيني) ولا يعمل شاهد إلخ: [ أي لا يشهد شاهد بخطه إذا رآه في الكتاب حتى يتذكر الحادثة. (عيني)] أي لا يجوز للشاهد إذا رأى خطه في صك أن يشهد إلا أن يتذكر الحادثة، وكذا القاضي إذا وجد في ديوانه إقرار رجل لرجل بحق من الحقوق وهو لا يتذكر الحادثة لا يحكم بذلك وكذا إذا وجد شهادة رجل يشهد لرجل آخر على رجل من الحقوق وهو لا يتذكر ذلك لا ينفذه حتى يتذكر، وكذا راوي الحديث إذا وجد الحديث مكتوباً بخطه أو بخط غيره، وهو معروف أنه قرأه على فلان لا يجوز له أن يحكم بالحل والحرمة بهذا الحديث حتى يتذكر الرواية، وهذا كله قول أبي حنيفة؛ لقوله علية: "إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد" شرط أن يكون عالماً، ولا يتصور العلم بدون تذكر الواقعة؛ لأن الخط يشبه الخط، فلا يلزم حجة؛
The book of testimony: [It is] like sale, acknowledgment, the judge's ruling, usurpation, and murder, even if he was not made a witness over it. And he may not testify to the testimony of another unless he was made a witness over it. And the witness of the effective [cause] does not act by itself, which is the condition; due to His statement, exalted: 'Except those who testify to the truth while they know' (al-Zukhruf 86). And it is better that he say: 'I testify that he sold, or acknowledged, or ruled, or usurped, or murdered'; because he directly witnessed the cause, so testifying to it became obligatory upon him. And he should not say: 'He made me witness' unless he actually made him witness, so that he not be a liar. And if he hears from behind a veil the acknowledgment of a person, it is not permissible for him to testify due to the possibility that it might be someone else, because voice resembles voice. Unless he entered the house and knew that there was no one else in it, then came out and sat at the door, and there is no other entrance to the house, and he heard the acknowledgment of the person in the house without seeing him, then at that time it is lawful for him to testify to his acknowledgment. It is appropriate for the judge, if he explains to him by saying 'I testify based on hearing from behind the veil', to accept the testimony. Do you not see that testimony by hearsay is only permitted in the six matters, as will come in the text. And they said: If he hears the voice of a woman from behind the veil, it is not permissible to testify against her, unless he sees her person. And a type [of testimony] whose ruling is not established by itself, like testimony upon testimony—if he hears someone testifying to something, it is not permissible for the listener to testify to his testimony unless he [the original] makes him a witness. And he alluded to this by his saying: 'and he may not testify to the testimony of another' etc. (Ayni, Fath, Inaya). 'As a witness': 'and even if he was not made a witness' meaning even if one of the owners of those contracts and rights and the judge did not make him a witness. (Ayni) 'over it': meaning over what occurred of speech or action. (Ayni) 'and he may not testify to the testimony of another' etc., because testimony is not effective by itself; rather it becomes effective only after transmission to the court. So agency and bearing [the testimony] are required, and they were not found, so it is not permissible. Similarly, if he heard someone else testifying to his testimony, it is not permissible for him to testify because he did not bear it; rather he bore [the testimony of] someone else. So it becomes analogous to the case where a person appoints an agent, where it is not permissible for the listener to act as long as he was not appointed, because the principal did not consent to his opinion. And acceptance of bearing [the testimony] and absence of subsequent prohibition are required. And it is restricted to testimony upon testimony because testimony based on the judge's ruling is valid even if the judge did not make him a witness over it, because the ruling is a binding proof, so it is lawful for him to testify to it. (Ayni, Fath) 'heard': 'as long as he was not made a witness' meaning as long as the witness did not say to him: 'Bear witness to my testimony'. (Ayni) 'and the witness does not act' etc.: [meaning a witness should not testify based on his handwriting when he sees it in a document unless he remembers the incident. (Ayni)] i.e., it is not permissible for a witness, when he sees his handwriting in a deed, to testify unless he remembers the incident. Similarly, the judge, if he finds in his register the acknowledgment of a man for a man of a right, and he does not remember the incident, he should not judge by it. Similarly, if he finds the testimony of a man testifying for another man against a man of a right, and he does not remember that, he should not enforce it until he remembers. Similarly, the hadith narrator, if he finds a hadith written in his handwriting or in another's, and it is known that he recited it to so-and-so, it is not permissible for him to rule by its permissibility or prohibition based on that hadith until he remembers the narration. And all of this is the saying of Abu Hanifa; due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'When you know it like the sun, then testify'—the condition is that he be knowledgeable, and knowledge is inconceivable without remembering the incident, because handwriting resembles handwriting, so it does not constitute a binding proof.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. It opens the Book of Testimony by stating that testimony is analogous to sale, acknowledgment, etc., meaning the same rules apply: the witness must have direct knowledge. The Quranic verse 'Except those who testify to the truth while they know' establishes the requirement of knowledge. The preferred wording for a witness is 'I testify that he sold' etc., directly stating the fact witnessed, rather than 'he made me witness' unless actually asked to bear witness. The passage then addresses a practical scenario: hearing an acknowledgment from behind a veil. Generally, it is not allowed due to possibility of mistaken identity unless one has verified the person's identity by entering the house and ensuring no one else is present. Similarly, hearing a woman's voice from behind a veil is insufficient unless the witness can see her person. Finally, the passage states that a person cannot testify on the testimony of another (i.e., second-hand testimony) unless the original witness formally appointed him. The commentary expands this by explaining that testimony only becomes effective when transmitted to court, so it requires agency (tahammul) which was absent. It also notes an exception: testimony regarding the judge's ruling is valid even without being made a witness, because the ruling itself is a binding proof. The passage concludes with Abu Hanifa's position on acting on handwriting: recollection of the event is necessary, as per the hadith 'When you know it like the sun, then testify'.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Giving testimony in court about a right or fact that the witness has directly witnessed.
التسامع (al-tasammu'): Hearsay testimony where the witness reports what he heard from others without direct observation.
التحمل (al-tahammul): The act of bearing testimony, i.e., being present at the event or being formally appointed to transmit the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who hears an acknowledgment from behind a veil without seeing the person?
A) He may testify because the Quran says 'except those who testify to the truth'.
B) He may not testify because of the possibility that the voice belongs to someone else.
C) He may testify only if the person is a relative.
D) He may testify if he later sees the person.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is only valid when based on certain knowledge, either through direct observation or verified identity; hearsay and unrecalled handwriting do not meet this standard.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Testifying Based on Handwriting
Disagreement among Hanafi imams on acting by handwriting without recollection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on acting upon handwriting, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Handwriting may replace memory for judges and narrators if security from forgery exists, but not for witnesses.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a judge, hadith narrator, or witness can rely on written records without personal recollection. Abu Hanifa requires direct memory, while the two Sahibayn allow it under certain conditions. The practical consequence affects court procedure and hadith transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their roles
The passage discusses three roles: judge (qadi), narrator (rawi), and witness (shahid). Each has a different relationship to written records.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa requires recollection in all cases; handwriting alone is insufficient because it is susceptible to forgery.
This is the strictest view.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf allows the judge and narrator to rely on handwriting because their records are secure, but the witness cannot because the deed is in the hands of litigants.
He distinguishes based on the security of the document.
4
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani allows anyone to act on handwriting if they are certain of its authenticity, even without recollection, as a facilitation.
This is the relied-upon fatwa.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states 'upon it is the fatwa' referring to Muhammad's view for judges and narrators. The witness remains restricted.
The witness cannot rely on handwriting even if certain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقاض وراو بالخط إن لم يتذكروا، ولا يشهد بما لم يعاينه إلا النسب.
****
يرجع إلى الكل كما ذكرنا أحد لاحتمال التزوير، وقال محمد: يجوز لكل واحد منهم أن يعمل بالكتاب إن تيقن به، وإن لم يتذكر الواقعة توسعة للأمر على الناس وعليه الفتوى وقال أبو يوسف يجوز للراوي أن يعمل بالخط لدلالة الظاهر، وكذا للقاضي أن يحكم بالشهادة وأن يمضي القضاء بذلك، وليس للشاهد أن يشهد برؤية خطه ما لم يتذكر الشهادة؛ لأن سجل القاضي في خريطة، وهي في يده تحت ختمه، فيؤمن من التبديل والتغيير، وكتابة الرواية محفوظ تحت يد الراوي فيؤمن أيضاً من التزوير، بخلاف كتابة الشاهد؛ لأن الصك يكون في أيدي الخصم فلا يؤمن من التبديل رمز الحقائق: ١٤٢/٢] وعلى هذا الاختلاف إذا تذكر المجلس الذي كانت فيه الشهادة أو أخبره قوم ممن يثق بهم إنا شهدنا نحن وأنت، فإنه قيل: يحل له الشهادة بالاتفاق، وقيل: لا يحل عند الإمام، خلافاً لهما. (عيني، فتح، عناية) وقاض: أي ولا يحكم قاض إذا وجد في ديوانه مكتوبا شهادة شهود ولا يحفظ أنهم شهود بذلك. (عيني) وراو بالخط أي ولا يروي راوي الحديث إذا وجد مكتوبا بخط، فليس له أن يروي حتى يتذكر الرواية. (عيني) إن لم يتذكروا هؤلاء أي شاهدان إن لم يتذكرا الشهادة والقاضي إن لم يتذكر القضية، والراوي إن لم يتذكر الرواية. (عيني)
And a judge and a narrator [acting] by handwriting if they do not remember. And he may not testify to what he did not directly witness except [in matters of] lineage.
****
It refers back to all as we mentioned, one due to the possibility of forgery. And Muhammad said: It is permissible for each one of them to act upon the book if he is certain of it, even if he does not remember the incident, as a facilitation for people, and upon it is the fatwa. And Abu Yusuf said: It is permissible for the narrator to act upon the handwriting due to the indication of the apparent, and similarly for the judge to judge by the testimony and to execute the ruling by that. But it is not for the witness to testify upon seeing his handwriting unless he remembers the testimony, because the judge's record is in a pouch, in his hand under his seal, so it is safe from alteration and change. And the writing of the narration is preserved under the hand of the narrator, so it is also safe from forgery, unlike the writing of the witness because the deed is in the hands of the litigant, so it is not safe from alteration. (Raml al-Haqa'iq 142/2) And upon this difference, if he remembers the assembly in which the testimony occurred, or a trustworthy group informs him that 'we and you testified', then it is said: it is lawful for him to testify by agreement, and it is said: it is not lawful according to the Imam, contrary to them two. (Ayni, Fath, Inaya) 'And a judge': meaning he should not judge if he finds in his register written testimony of witnesses and he does not recall that they are witnesses by that. (Ayni) 'And a narrator by handwriting': meaning the hadith narrator should not narrate if he finds it written by handwriting; he should not narrate until he remembers the narration. (Ayni) 'If they do not remember': these, i.e., the two witnesses if they do not remember the testimony, and the judge if he does not remember the case, and the narrator if he does not remember the narration. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether a judge, narrator (of hadith), or witness can act based solely on written records without remembering the event. The matn states that a judge or narrator should not act on handwriting if they do not remember; also, one cannot testify to what he did not directly witness except in lineage (this second part will be expanded later). The commentary explains the dispute: Abu Hanifa's position (implied from the previous lesson) requires recollection in all cases. Muhammad al-Shaybani permits acting on a written record if one is certain of its authenticity, even without recollection, as a facilitation for people—and this is the relied-upon fatwa. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: he allows the narrator to rely on handwriting (since his own copies are under his control) and the judge to rely on court records (since they are sealed and secure), but the witness cannot rely on his handwriting in a deed because the deed is in the hands of the litigant and prone to forgery. The commentary then discusses a scenario: if the witness remembers the court session or is informed by trustworthy people that they together testified, then there is disagreement: some say he can testify by consensus, while according to Abu Hanifa he may not, unlike Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The passage then provides literal explanations of the terms: 'judge' refers to the judge who finds written testimony in his register but does not remember it; 'narrator by handwriting' refers to the hadith narrator who finds a written hadith; 'if they do not remember' applies to witnesses, judge, and narrator.

Key Terms
وقاض وراو (wa qadin wa rawin): Judge and narrator (of hadith). The matn addresses both as persons who may rely on written records.
بالخط (bil-khatt): By handwriting; i.e., acting upon written records without independent recollection.
سجل القاضي (sijill al-qādī): The judge's record or register, which is sealed and under his control.
خريطة (kharīṭa): Pouch or bag used to store the judge's documents, metaphor for secure storage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi), when can a judge act upon a written testimony found in his register?
A) Only if he remembers the testimony.
B) Never, because handwriting is unreliable.
C) If he is certain of the handwriting, even without remembering.
D) Only if there are two witnesses to the register.

Key Takeaway
A judge and narrator may rely on handwriting if certain of its authenticity, but a witness must always remember the event.

Exceptions to Direct Observation: Hearsay Testimony Allowed
Lists the six matters where hearsay testimony is accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six matters where hearsay testimony is accepted and apply the Hanafi conditions for each.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is generally rejected; only six specific matters are excepted due to necessity.

Islamic court testimony normally requires direct observation. The Hanafi school, however, recognizes that some facts – like lineage, death, and endowments – are often established through public knowledge. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the six matters where hearsay (tasammu') is accepted, along with important conditions and a dispute within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage begins by affirming that testimony by hearsay is not allowed because knowledge (ilm) is a condition for testimony. Understand the foundational principle: one cannot testify to what one did not directly witness.
The rule is based on consensus (ijma).
2
List the six exceptions
The text mentions lineage (nasab), death (mawt), killing (qatl), marriage (nikah implied), and original endowment (asl al-waqf). Some sources count six including marriage. Identify each exception from the passage.
Marriage is not explicitly listed but is commonly included.
3
Analyze conditions for each exception
For lineage, the judge only accepts after a claim of maintenance or inheritance, except for father-son. For death, there are restrictions based on the notability of the deceased. For endowment, only the origin is accepted, not its conditions; the beneficiary must be specified. Note these conditions.
The conditions ensure reliability.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on wala'
Abu Yusuf extends the exception to clientage (wala') by analogy with lineage. The majority rejects this because wala' involves removal of ownership, which requires direct observation.
The relied-upon position restricts to six matters.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that hearsay testimony is accepted only in the six specified matters. This is the position for fatwa.
Other schools may differ, but Hanafis adhere to this strict list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بما لم يعاينه بالإجماع؛ لأن العلم شرط أداء الشهادة فلا يجوز أن يشهد بشيء و لم يعاينه بالتسامع. (عيني، عناية) إلا النسب بأن سمع من الناس أن فلاناً ابن فلان أو أخوه يسعه أن يشهد بذلك. (عيني)] والحاصل أن الشهود إذا شهدوا بنسب، فإن القاضي لا يقبلهم ولا يحكم بالنسب إلا بعد دعوى النفقة أو الإرث، إلا في الأب والابن. وقوله: "والموت" ظاهر إطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين كون الميت مشهوراً أو لا، وقيده في "المعراج" بأن يكون عالماً أو من العمال، فإن كان تاجراً أو نحوه، فإنه لا يجوز إلا بالمعاينة، والقتل كالموت، وقيل: في الموت يكتفي بإخبار واحد عدل أو واحدة؛ لأنه قد يتحقق في موضع ليس فيه إلا واحد بخلاف غيره، وعند الثلاثة لابد من اثنين عدلين.
وقوله: "وأصل الوقف احترز به عن شرائطه؛ لأن أصل الوقف هو الذي يشتهر دون شرائطه، فلا تقبل الشهادة فيها بالتسامع، وذكر المرغيناني أنه لابد من بيان الجهة بأن يشهدوا أنه وقف على هذا المسجد أو المقبرة أو الفقراء وما أشبهه، حتى لو لم يذكروا في شهادتهم الجهة لا تقبل شهادتهم، ومعناه أنهم بعد ما ذكروا أن هذا وقف على كذا، لا ينبغي لهم أن يشهدوا أنه يبدأ من غلته فيصرف إلى كذا حتى لو قالوا ذلك في شهادتهم، لا تقبل، ثم قصر الاستثناء على هذه الأشياء الستة إشارة إلى أنه لا يجوز أن يشهدوا بالتسامع في غيرها، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه يجوز في الولاء أيضاً اعتباراً بالنسب؛ لأن الولاء بمنزلته، ولنا أنه يبتني على زوال الملك، ولابد فيه من المعاينة، فكذا ما يبتني عليه والشهادة بالعتق بالتسامع لا تقبل بالإجماع. (عيني، فتح)
By what he did not directly witness by consensus; because knowledge is a condition for performing testimony, so it is not permissible to testify to something that he did not directly witness by hearsay. (Ayni, Inaya) Except [in] lineage, such that he heard from people that so-and-so is the son of so-and-so or his brother, he may testify to that. (Ayni) The gist is that if witnesses testify to lineage, the judge does not accept them and does not judge by lineage except after a claim of maintenance or inheritance, except regarding the father and son. And his statement: 'And death' - its apparent absolute [meaning] is that there is no difference between the deceased being well-known or not. But it was restricted in al-Mi'raj to being a scholar or an official; if he was a merchant or the like, then it is not permissible except by direct observation. And killing is like death. And it was said: regarding death, the report of one upright man or woman suffices, because it may occur in a place where there is only one person, unlike others. And according to the three, two upright persons are necessary. And his statement: 'And the origin of endowment'—he restricted it to its conditions because the origin of endowment (asl al-waqf) is what is well-known, unlike its conditions, so testimony by hearsay is not accepted regarding them. And al-Marghinani mentioned that it is necessary to specify the beneficiary (jihah) such that they testify that it is an endowment upon this mosque, or cemetery, or the poor, and the like, such that if they did not mention in their testimony the beneficiary, their testimony is not accepted. Its meaning is that after they mention that this is an endowment for such-and-such, they should not testify that 'its proceeds begin and are spent on such-and-such'; even if they say that in their testimony, it is not accepted. Then he restricted the exception to these six matters, indicating that it is not permissible to testify by hearsay in other than them. And it is reported from Abu Yusuf that it is also permissible in wala' (clientage) by analogy with lineage, because wala' is like lineage. Our [proof] is that it is based on removal of ownership, and direct observation is necessary for it; likewise for what it is based on. And testimony by hearsay regarding manumission (itq) is not accepted by consensus. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling that testimony by hearsay (tasammu') is generally not allowed, with exceptions. It begins by affirming the principle: knowledge is a condition for testimony, so one cannot testify to what he did not directly witness. Then it lists the exceptions, which are commonly six: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), killing (qatl), marriage (nikah) (though not explicitly mentioned here, it is implied as part of the six), and original endowment (asl al-waqf). The passage elaborates on lineage: the judge only accepts such testimony after a claim of maintenance or inheritance, except for the father and son relationship. For death, there is a difference: some restrict it to well-known persons or those whose death is likely, while others allow it generally. The testimony of a single upright person may suffice in remote places. For killing, similar rules apply. For endowment, only the original establishment of the waqf can be testified by hearsay, not its detailed conditions; also the beneficiary must be specified. The passage ends with a note that Abu Yusuf extends the exception to wala' (clientage) by analogy with lineage, but the text rejects this because wala' is based on removal of ownership, which requires direct observation. The Hanafi position is that testimony by hearsay is limited to these specific matters.

Key Terms
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage; family relationship. One may testify to it based on common knowledge and hearsay.
التسامع (al-tasammu'): Hearsay; reporting what one has heard from others without direct observation.
الولاء (al-wala'): Clientage; the bond of loyalty between a freed slave and his former master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, in which of the following matters is testimony by hearsay (tasammu') permitted?
A) Lineage and wala'
B) Death and lineage only
C) The six matters including marriage, death, and original endowment
D) Any matter that is well-known among people

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is strictly limited to six matters in Hanafi law; each comes with specific conditions that must be satisfied for the testimony to be accepted.

Testimony Based on Handwriting and the Exception for Lineage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on handwriting-based testimony and hearsay exception for lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on acting on handwriting without memory, identify the mufta bihi, and explain why lineage is excepted from the requirement of direct observation.

Core Idea
Acting on handwriting without memory is disputed; the facilitation view prevails, and lineage is an exception to direct testimony.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses when a judge, narrator, or witness may rely on written records without memory. It also establishes a key exception: lineage can be testified by hearsay. The text then elaborates on the intra-Hanafi dispute, with Imam Muhammad's view adopted as the operative position due to necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the core issue
Recognize that the ruling concerns three roles: judge, narrator (of hadith), and witness. The issue is whether they can act based solely on handwriting when they do not remember the original event.
The matn says 'if they do not remember' – memory is the default requirement.
2
Examine the three intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa disallows all; Muhammad allows all if certain of the handwriting; Abu Yusuf allows only judge and narrator. Understand each rationale: forgery risk vs. facilitation vs. document security.
Muhammad's view is based on tawsi'ah (facilitation) for people.
3
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The later school adopted Muhammad's view. The practical effect: if the judge or narrator is certain of the handwriting, they may act even without memory.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and others rule accordingly.
4
Analyze the exception for lineage
The general rule forbids testifying to what one has not witnessed directly. Lineage is excepted because it is necessarily known by hearsay. However, the judge only rules on lineage after a claim of maintenance or inheritance, except for father-son.
This exception is by consensus (ijma').

Source Text

(عيني، فتح، عناية) وقاض: أي ولا يحكم قاض إذا وجد في ديوانه مكتوبا شهادة شهود ولا يحفظ أنهم شهود بذلك. (عيني) وراو بالخط أي ولا يروي راوي الحديث إذا وجد مكتوبا بخط، فليس له أن يروي حتى يتذكر الرواية. (عيني) إن لم يتذكروا هؤلاء أي شاهدان إن لم يتذكرا الشهادة والقاضي إن لم يتذكر القضية، والراوي إن لم يتذكر الرواية. (عيني) بما لم يعاينه بالإجماع؛ لأن العلم شرط أداء الشهادة فلا يجوز أن يشهد بشيء و لم يعاينه بالتسامع. (عيني، عناية) إلا النسب بأن سمع من الناس أن فلاناً ابن فلان أو أخوه يسعه أن يشهد بذلك. (عيني)] والحاصل أن الشهود إذا شهدوا بنسب، فإن القاضي لا يقبلهم ولا يحكم بالنسب إلا بعد دعوى النفقة أو الإرث، إلا في الأب والابن.
This is the book of testimony and what pertains to it. A judge and a narrator [cannot act] based on handwriting if they do not remember. And one should not testify to what he has not witnessed except lineage. It goes back to all as we mentioned. One [says: it is not allowed] due to possibility of forgery. Muhammad said: Each of them may act based on the writing if he is certain of it, even if he does not remember the event, as a facilitation for people, and upon this is the fatwa. Abu Yusuf said: The narrator may act based on handwriting due to apparent evidence, and likewise the judge may pass judgment based on testimony and execute the judgment accordingly, but the witness may not testify based on seeing his own handwriting unless he remembers the testimony. Because the judge's record is in a folder under his seal and is safe from alteration, and the narration is preserved under the narrator's hand, also safe from forgery, unlike the witness's writing because the document is in the hands of the litigants and not safe from alteration. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:142). And regarding this difference if he remembers the session in which the testimony was given or a trustworthy group informs him 'we and you testified', it is said: it is permissible for him to testify by agreement, and it is said: it is not permissible according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], contrary to them the two. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inaya). 'And a judge' i.e. a judge should not judge if he finds in his register written testimony of witnesses and does not remember that they were witnesses for that. ('Ayni). 'And a narrator by handwriting' i.e. a hadith narrator should not narrate if he finds something written, until he remembers the narration. ('Ayni). 'If they do not remember' these three: two witnesses if they do not remember the testimony, the judge if he does not remember the case, and the narrator if he does not remember the narration. ('Ayni). 'Should not testify to what he has not witnessed' by consensus, because knowledge is a condition for performing testimony, so it is not permissible to testify to something he has not witnessed by hearsay. ('Ayni, 'Inaya). 'Except lineage' such as hearing from people that so-and-so is the son of so-and-so or his brother, it is permissible for him to testify to that. ('Ayni). The summary: if witnesses testify to lineage, the judge should not accept them and not rule on lineage except after a claim of maintenance or inheritance, except in the case of father and son.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on testimony based on handwriting and the intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that a judge and narrator cannot rely on handwriting without memory, and that one should not testify to what he has not witnessed except for lineage. The commentary explains the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa disallows all except lineage, while Muhammad allows acting on handwriting if certain, and Abu Yusuf allows for judge and narrator but not witness. The relied-upon position is Muhammad's as a dispensation. The exception for lineage is by consensus.

Key Terms
الخط (al-khatt): Handwriting; the written record of testimony, judgment, or narration
التسامع (al-tasammu'): Hearsay; hearing from others without direct observation
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage; family relationship by blood

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must be certain of the handwriting, even without memory
C) He must have two witnesses confirm the record
D) He may act only if the record is under his seal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits acting on handwriting without memory if one is certain of the handwriting, as a facilitation; lineage is an exception to the requirement of direct observation.

Shahadat — Testimony

Hearsay Testimony on Six Matters: Conditions and the Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Six matters where hearsay testimony is permissible with conditions and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six matters where hearsay testimony is permitted, state the conditions for its acceptance, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of required informants.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is allowed on six specific matters by istihsan, with a dispute on the degree of certainty required.

The Hanafi school permits hearsay testimony (shahada bi al-tasamu') on six matters due to necessity, despite the general rule requiring direct observation. This lesson explores those six matters, the conditions for acceptance, and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of informants needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six exceptional matters
From the matn, list the six matters: death, marriage, entry (dakhul), appointment of a judge, origin of a waqf, and (indirectly) the possession of property (except slaves).
The six are enumerated in the matn and expanded by the commentary.
2
Understand the general condition of knowledge
The witness must have acquired knowledge (ilm) of the matter through tawatur (widespread report), the report of two just men or one man and two women, or from a trustworthy person (by istihsan).
This condition is derived from the commentary's explanation of the matn.
3
Note the specific conditions for death and waqf
For death, the deceased must be well-known or a scholar/functionary; for a merchant, direct observation is required. For waqf, the beneficiary direction (jihah) must be specified in the testimony.
These conditions are from the commentary's refinement of the matn's apparent generality.
4
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
Qiyas would disallow hearsay testimony entirely, but istihsan permits it on these six matters to prevent hardship (haraj) and to preserve rulings over time.
The argument is dalil aqli: the necessity outweighs the general prohibition.
5
Compare the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa requires general public reputation that causes certainty; the Sahibayn accept the report of two just men or one man and two women. The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn for ease of practice.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the text declares the Sahibayn's view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: "والموت" ظاهر إطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين كون الميت مشهوراً أو لا، وقيده في "المعراج" بأن يكون عالماً أو من العمال، فإن كان تاجراً أو نحوه، فإنه لا يجوز إلا بالمعاينة، والقتل كالموت، وقيل: في الموت يكتفي بإخبار واحد عدل أو واحدة؛ لأنه قد يتحقق في موضع ليس فيه إلا واحد بخلاف غيره، وعند الثلاثة لابد من اثنين عدلين.
وقوله: "وأصل الوقف احترز به عن شرائطه؛ لأن أصل الوقف هو الذي يشتهر دون شرائطه، فلا تقبل الشهادة فيها بالتسامع، وذكر المرغيناني أنه لابد من بيان الجهة بأن يشهدوا أنه وقف على هذا المسجد أو المقبرة أو الفقراء وما أشبهه، حتى لو لم يذكروا في شهادتهم الجهة لا تقبل شهادتهم، ومعناه أنهم بعد ما ذكروا أن هذا وقف على كذا، لا ينبغي لهم أن يشهدوا أنه يبدأ من غلته فيصرف إلى كذا حتى لو قالوا ذلك في شهادتهم، لا تقبل، ثم قصر الاستثناء على هذه الأشياء الستة إشارة إلى أنه لا يجوز أن يشهدوا بالتسامع في غيرها، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه يجوز في الولاء أيضاً اعتباراً بالنسب؛ لأن الولاء بمنزلته، ولنا أنه يبتني على زوال الملك، ولابد فيه من المعاينة، فكذا ما يبتني عليه والشهادة بالعتق بالتسامع لا تقبل بالإجماع. (عيني، فتح)
كتاب الشهادة
٤٤٦
الشهادة وما يتعلق بها
والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضي وأصل الوقف، فله أن يشهد بها إذا فللشاهد أخبره بها من يثق به. ومن في يده شيء سوى الرقيق لك أن تشهد أنه له، الشاهد بهذه الأشياء : بهذه الأشياء الستة أي وسع لك أي ذلك الشيء لمن في يده
والموت بأن سمع من الناس أن فلاناً قد مات يسعه أن يشهد. (عيني، معدن) والنكاح: بأن سمع أن المرأة الفلانة منكوحة فلان أن يسعه يشهد بالنكاح ولو لم يعاينه (عيني) والدخول بأن سمع أن فلاناً تزوج فلانة ودخل بها يسعه أن يشهد بذلك. (معدن) وولاية القاضي: بأن سمع أن فلانا قد تولى القضاء من جهة فلان الإمام يسعه أن يشهد. (معدن) وأصل الوقف بأن سمع أن فلانا وقف هذه الضيعة يسعه أن يشهد. (معدن) إذا أخبره يدل على أن لفظ الشهادة ليست بشرط في الكل أما الذي يشهد عند القاضي، فلابد من لفظها، ثم الشاهد بهذه الأشياء إنما يجوز شهادته إذا حصل له العلم بها، إما بالتواتر أو بإخبار رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، أو بإخبار من يثق به استحساناً، والقياس أن لا تجوز الشهادة بالتسامع في شيء؛ لأنها بلا علم ولا مشاهدة، وجه الاستحسان أن هذه الأمور يختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون والأعصار، فلو لم تقبل الشهادة فيها بالتسامع، لأدّى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام من يثق به: العدد فيه شرط، وهو أن يخبره رجلان عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان ليحصل له نوع علم، وهذا على قولهما، وأما على قول أبي حنيفة، فلا تجوز الشهادة ما لم يسمع ذلك من العامة بحيث يقع في قلبه صدق الخبر. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
His saying: 'and death' - its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between the deceased being well-known or not, but it is restricted in al-Mi'raj to a scholar or a functionary; if he is a merchant or similar, it is not allowed except by direct observation. Killing is like death. And it is said: in death, the report of one just man or one just woman suffices because it may occur in a place where there is only one person, unlike other matters. According to the three, two just men are required. His saying: 'and the origin of the endowment' - by this he excludes its conditions; because the origin of the endowment is what is well-known, not its conditions, so testimony therein by hearsay is not accepted. Al-Marghinani mentioned that it is necessary to specify the beneficiary direction, so they testify that it is an endowment for this mosque, cemetery, poor, etc. If they do not mention the direction, their testimony is not accepted. The meaning is that after mentioning that it is an endowment for such and such, they should not testify that from its revenue it is spent on such and such; if they say that in their testimony, it is not accepted. Then the restriction of the exception to these six matters indicates that they should not testify by hearsay in other matters. From Abu Yusuf: it is also permissible in wala' (clientage) by analogy to lineage because wala' is like lineage. But our proof: it is based on transfer of ownership, and direct observation is required, so likewise what is based on it. Testimony by hearsay about emancipation is not accepted by consensus. ('Ayni, Fath). Book of Testimony, page 446. Testimony and what pertains to it: and death, marriage, entry, the appointment of a judge, and the origin of an endowment, so he is allowed to testify to them if someone he trusts informs him. And from 'whoever has something in his hand except slaves, you may testify that it is his.' The witness regarding these matters: about these six things, i.e., it is permissible for you to testify that this thing belongs to the one in whose hand it is. Death: if he hears from people that so-and-so has died, he may testify. ('Ayni, Ma'din). Marriage: if he hears that such a woman is married to so-and-so, he may testify to the marriage even if he did not witness it. ('Ayni). Entry: if he hears that so-and-so married so-and-so and entered (consummated) with her, he may testify. (Ma'din). Appointment of judge: if he hears that so-and-so was appointed as judge by such an imam, he may testify. (Ma'din). Origin of endowment: if he hears that so-and-so endowed this land, he may testify. (Ma'din). 'If he informs him' indicates that the wording of testimony is not required in all cases; as for one who testifies before a judge, the wording is necessary. Then the witness in these matters is allowed to testify only if he has acquired knowledge of them, either through tawatur (widespread report) or the report of two men or one man and two women, or the report of someone he trusts by istihsan. The qiyas is that testimony by hearsay in anything is not permissible because it is without knowledge or observation. The justification for istihsan is that these matters are such that only certain people witness their causes, yet rulings remain over time. If testimony by hearsay were not accepted, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings. 'From someone he trusts': number is a condition: that two just men or one man and two women inform him to attain some knowledge; this is according to them (the two). According to Abu Hanifa, testimony is not allowed unless he hears it from the general public such that he becomes certain of the truth. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inaya).
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage explains the six matters where hearsay testimony is exceptional. The matn lists death, marriage, entry (dakhul), appointment of judge, and the original establishment of a waqf. The commentary discusses conditions: the witness must have knowledge, either through widespread report (tawatur) or information from two just men or one man and two women, or from a trustworthy person by istihsan. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa requires general reputation causing certainty, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) accept the report of two men or one man and two women. The relied-upon position is that of the two. The istihsan is based on preventing hardship and preserving rulings over time.

Key Terms
الإستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling due to necessity
التواتر (al-tawatur): Widespread report that yields certain knowledge due to the number and reliability of reporters
الجهة (al-jihah): The beneficiary direction of a waqf (e.g., mosque, poor) that must be specified in testimony

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two just men or one man and two women

D) A large group causing certainty

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows hearsay testimony on six matters based on the report of two just men or one man and two women, by istihsan.

Testimony by Possession: The Rule and the Dispute
Ruling that possession is evidence of ownership for testimony, except for slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that possession is evidence of ownership for testimony, identify the exception for slaves, and evaluate the condition of public dealing (tasarruf) as the chosen view.

Core Idea
Possession is the ultimate proof of ownership for testimony, unless possession is improbable or the property is a slave who can speak.

In Islamic courts, testimony often requires direct eyewitness evidence. But for ownership, what if you simply see someone holding a thing? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that possession (yad) is valid basis for testifying that the property belongs to the possessor, with important exceptions and a debated condition of public dealing (tasarruf). We will walk through the reasoning, the exception for slaves, and the preferred view among Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the matn: 'you may testify that it is his' when you see something in someone's hand. State the general rule and the exception for slaves.
The exception is for slaves known to be slaves because they can speak for themselves.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The commentary gives a rational proof: possession is the ultimate reference because all chains of ownership trace back to it. Understand why this is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
Without possession, the door of testimony would be closed – an argument by necessity.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the condition of Abu Yusuf (firm belief) and the condition of al-Khassaf (public dealing/tasarruf). Identify which is the chosen view (mukhtar).
The text says 'it is said: this is the chosen view' referring to al-Khassaf's condition.
4
Apply the rule to the street sweeper example
The street sweeper with a pearl: even with possession, testimony is not allowed because it is improbable. This shows the rule has a reasonableness condition.
This is linked to Abu Yusuf's requirement of firm belief and the general principle that improbable possession is not sufficient.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical consequence: with tasarruf, testimony is accepted; without it, some judges may reject the testimony. The mukhtar (chosen) view requires tasarruf.
This affects how a mufti or judge advises witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع شيء: كان ء: أي شيء من النقود والعروض والعقار. (عيني) سوى الرقيق ذكرا كان أو أنثى الذي علم رقه، ويعبر عن نفسه، وإلا فهو كمتاع. (ط، عيني) لك أن تشهد أنه له أي إذا رأيت شيئاً في يد شخص جاز لك أن تشهد أن ذلك الشيء لمن في يده؛ لأن اليد بلا منازع أقصى ما يستدل به على الملك؛ إذ هي مرجع الدلالة في الأسباب كلها، فإن الإنسان إذا عاين البيع لا يعلم ملك المشتري إلا بملك البائع، وملك البائع لا يعلم إلا باليد وأقصى ما يستدل به كاف في الشهادة، فإنها إذا لم تجز بحكم اليد انسد بابها، وهو مفتوح بالإجماع، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه يشترط ذلك أن يقع في قلبه أن الشيء ملك لذي اليد؛ ليحصل له نوع علم أو غلبة ظن. ولهذا قيل: لو رأى درة ثمينة في يد كناس أو كتاباً في يد جاهل وليس في آبائه من هو أهل لذلك، لا يسعه أن يشهد له، وشرط "الخصاف" التصرف مع اليد، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد، قيل: هو المختار، وعن مالك: لا تقبل في مدة يسيرة وتقبل في طويلة كعشر سنين، وشرط النسفي التصرف مع اليد وأن يقع في قلبه أنه له. ثم المسألة على أربعة أوجه الأول: أن يعاين المالك بأن عرفه باسمه ونسبه ووجهه وعرف الملك بحدوده، ورآه في يده بلا منازعة أحد، ثم رآه في يد غيره فجاء الأول وادعى الملك وسعه أن يشهد للأول بالملك بناء على يده، والثاني:
أن يعاين الملك بحدوده، وينسب إلى فلان ابن فلان ولم يعرفه بوجهه ونسبه، ثم جاء الذي نسب إليه لملك،
=
With something: any item of money, goods, or land. ('Ayni). Except slaves, male or female, whose slavery is known and who can speak for themselves; otherwise, it is like merchandise. (T, 'Ayni). You may testify that it is his: i.e., if you see something in a person's hand, you may testify that that thing belongs to the one in whose hand it is; because possession without dispute is the strongest evidence of ownership; it is the ultimate reference in all causes. For if one witnesses a sale, he does not know the buyer's ownership except through the seller's ownership, and the seller's ownership is known only through possession. The strongest evidence suffices for testimony; if testimony were not allowed based on possession, its door would be closed, whereas it is open by consensus. From Abu Yusuf: he requires that he firmly believe that the thing is the possessor's, to achieve some knowledge or predominant conjecture. Hence it is said: if he sees a precious pearl in the hand of a street sweeper, or a book in the hand of an ignorant person with no scholarly ancestors, he should not testify for him. Al-Khassaf conditioned public dealing (tasarruf) with possession, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad concur; it is said this is the chosen view. From Malik: not accepted for a short period but accepted for a long one like ten years. Al-Nasafi conditioned public dealing with possession and that he firmly believes it is his. Then the issue has four aspects: First: he witnessed the owner by name, lineage, and face, and knew the property by boundaries, and saw it in his hand without dispute; then he saw it in another's hand; the first comes and claims ownership; he may testify for the first based on his possession. Second: he witnessed the property boundaries and attributed it to so-and-so, but did not know him by face or lineage; then the one attributed to came to claim ownership, (incomplete).
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage establishes that possession (yad) is a valid basis for testimony of ownership. The matn allows testifying for the possessor of any property except slaves, because slaves can speak for themselves. The commentary explains the reasoning: the hand is the ultimate evidence of ownership, as all ownership is traced back to possession. Without this, testimony would be impossible. However, there are conditions: the possessor should be one who could reasonably own it (not a street sweeper with a pearl). Al-Khassaf adds the condition that the possessor publicly deals with the property (tasarruf), which is the relied-upon view. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf requires firm belief. The text also outlines four scenarios showing when testimony based on possession is acceptable, though the fourth is cut off.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): Possession; the fact that property is in someone's hand, indicating ownership
التصرف (al-tasarruf): Public dealing; the possessor's visible control and management of the property, such as selling or renting
الرقيق (al-raqiq): Slaves; they are excluded from the rule because they can speak for themselves about their ownership status

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (al-mukhtar), what additional condition did al-Khassaf require beyond possession for testimony of ownership?
A) The property must be immovable
B) The possessor must be a free adult
C) Public dealing (tasarruf) with the property
D) Two witnesses to the possession

Key Takeaway
Possession (yad) is a valid basis for testimony of ownership, but the chosen Hanafi view requires possession plus public dealing (tasarruf), and improbable possession is not accepted.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony by Hearsay for Six Matters
Ruling on permissibility of testifying by hearsay for six matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six matters for which hearsay testimony is permissible and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in these cases.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is permitted for six public matters to prevent hardship.

This passage from the Book of Testimony addresses a key exception: in certain matters of public knowledge, a witness may testify based on hearsay rather than direct observation. The Hanafi school employs istihsan to avoid the hardship that would arise if only eyewitness testimony were accepted for events like death and marriage. The ruling also highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute about the number of reporters needed for knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six matters
List the six types of cases where hearsay testimony is allowed: death, marriage, entry (consummation), appointment of a judge, origin of an endowment, and ownership of property (excluding slaves). These are public events that are difficult to directly observe.
2
Understand the condition of knowledge
The witness must have actual knowledge (ilm) of the matter. This knowledge can come through tawatur (widespread report), or the report of two men or one man and two women (Sahibayn), or a single trustworthy person (Abu Hanifa).
The intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the number of reporters required.
3
Distinguish qiyas from istihsan
Qiyas would require direct observation for all testimony. Istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid hardship (haraj) because these matters are essential and would be impossible to prove by eyewitness alone across generations.
The illa for istihsan is necessity.
4
Note the practical consequence
The difference between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn affects cases where only one reliable person reports. Abu Hanifa accepts; Sahibayn does not. The mufta bihi is typically Sahibayn's view.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a modern scenario (e.g., hearing of a death from neighbors), determine whether testimony is accepted and under which condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة الشهادة وما يتعلق بها والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضي وأصل الوقف، فله أن يشهد بها إذا أخبره بها من يثق به. ومن في يده شيء سوى الرقيق لك أن تشهد أنه له، فللشاهد بهذه الأشياء : بهذه الأشياء الستة أي وسع لك أي ذلك الشيء لمن في يده والموت بأن سمع من الناس أن فلاناً قد مات يسعه أن يشهد. (عيني، معدن) والنكاح: بأن سمع أن المرأة الفلانة منكوحة فلان أن يسعه يشهد بالنكاح ولو لم يعاينه (عيني) والدخول بأن سمع أن فلاناً تزوج فلانة ودخل بها يسعه أن يشهد بذلك. (معدن) وولاية القاضي: بأن سمع أن فلانا قد تولى القضاء من جهة فلان الإمام يسعه أن يشهد. (معدن) وأصل الوقف بأن سمع أن فلانا وقف هذه الضيعة يسعه أن يشهد. (معدن) إذا أخبره يدل على أن لفظ الشهادة ليست بشرط في الكل أما الذي يشهد عند القاضي، فلابد من لفظها، ثم الشاهد بهذه الأشياء إنما يجوز شهادته إذا حصل له العلم بها، إما بالتواتر أو بإخبار رجلين أو رجل وامرأتين، أو بإخبار من يثق به استحساناً، والقياس أن لا تجوز الشهادة بالتسامع في شيء؛ لأنها بلا علم ولا مشاهدة، وجه الاستحسان أن هذه الأمور يختص بمعاينة أسبابها خواص من الناس ويتعلق بها أحكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون والأعصار، فلو لم تقبل الشهادة فيها بالتسامع، لأدّى إلى الحرج وتعطيل الأحكام من يثق به: العدد فيه شرط، وهو أن يخبره رجلان عدلان أو رجل وامرأتان ليحصل له نوع علم، وهذا على قولهما، وأما على قول أبي حنيفة، فلا تجوز الشهادة ما لم يسمع ذلك من العامة بحيث يقع في قلبه صدق الخبر. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
Book of Testimony. Testimony and what pertains to it. Death, marriage, entry, appointment of a judge, and the origin of endowment: he may testify to them when he is informed by one he trusts. And whoever has something in his possession other than slaves, you may testify that it is his. For the witness, these things: these six things. That is, it is permissible for you that that thing is for the one in whose hand it is. Death: by hearing from the people that so-and-so has died, he may testify. (Ayni, Ma'dan) Marriage: by hearing that such a woman is the wife of such a man, he may testify to the marriage even if he did not witness it (Ayni). Entry: by hearing that so-and-so married such a woman and entered with her, he may testify to that. (Ma'dan) Appointment of the judge: by hearing that so-and-so has been appointed as judge by such an imam, he may testify. (Ma'dan) Origin of the endowment: by hearing that so-and-so endowed this estate, he may testify. (Ma'dan) 'When he informs him' indicates that the wording of testimony is not a condition for all. But as for one who testifies before the judge, the wording is necessary. Then the witness regarding these things: his testimony is only permitted if he has obtained knowledge of them, either through tawatur (continuous report), or by the report of two men or one man and two women, or by the report of one he trusts, by istihsan. Qiyas (analogy) dictates that testimony by hearsay should not be permissible in anything because it is without knowledge and observation. The reason for istihsan is that these matters have causes that are witnessed only by specific people, and rulings are attached to them that remain over the passing of centuries and ages. So if testimony by hearsay were not accepted, it would lead to hardship and the suspension of rulings. 'From one he trusts' – number is a condition in it, which is that two just men or one man and two women inform him so that he obtains some knowledge, and this according to them (Sahibayn). As for the view of Abu Hanifa, testimony is not permissible unless he hears it from the general public such that the truthfulness of the report settles in his heart. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Testimony on the permissibility of testifying by hearsay for six specific matters: death, marriage, entry (consummation), appointment of a judge, and the origin of an endowment. The author states that a witness may testify to these if he is informed by someone he trusts. The commentary explains that the six matters are listed, and for each, the condition is hearing from the public without direct observation. The key legal issue is that the witness must have actual knowledge (ilm), which can come through tawatur (widespread report), the testimony of two men or one man and two women, or even a single trustworthy person by way of istihsan. The passage contrasts this with qiyas, which would require direct observation for all testimony. The reason (illa) for the istihsan exception is that these matters—death, marriage, etc.—are public events that would be extremely difficult to prove if only eyewitness testimony were accepted, leading to hardship (haraj) and the suspension of rulings. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), number is a condition (two men or one man and two women), while Abu Hanifa requires that the witness hears it from the general public so that he becomes internally convinced. This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas to prevent hardship.

Key Terms
تسامع (tasāmu‘): Hearsay: information heard from the public without direct observation.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference: setting aside qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling to avoid hardship.
تواتر (tawātur): Continuous report from a large number that precludes collusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason (illa) for allowing testimony by hearsay for the six matters?
A) Because these matters are impossible to witness directly
B) To prevent hardship and suspension of rulings
C) Because the Quran explicitly permits it
D) Because the witness is always truthful

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hearsay testimony for six public matters based on istihsan to prevent hardship, distinguishing its conditions of knowledge.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony by Possession: General Rule and Conditions
Ruling on testimony by possession with conditions from Hanafi masters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that possession without dispute is evidence for testimony, and identify the conditions added by Abu Yusuf, al-Khassaf, and al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
Possession is the primary indicator of ownership; testimony based on it is permitted by consensus, but scholars differ on whether additional disposition or inner certainty is required.

This lesson unpacks the foundational Hanafi principle that seeing property in a person's hand without contest allows you to testify that it belongs to him. We will explore why this is so, and the varying conditions classical scholars placed on this testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is testifying that property belongs to the possessor. The ruling is that it is permissible (jāʾiz) based on possession without dispute.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is consensus (ijmāʿ) that the door of testimony remains open; otherwise, many rights would be lost.
The text states: 'فإنها إذا لم تجز بحكم اليد انسد بابها، وهو مفتوح بالإجماع'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
Possession without dispute is the strongest evidence of ownership. If it were not accepted, the entire system of proving ownership through testimony would break down.
The text compares to witnessing a sale: ownership is ultimately traced back to possession.
4
Note the ikhtilāf on conditions
Abū Yūsuf requires the witness to have inner conviction; al-Khassāf and al-Shāfiʿī/Aḥmad require disposition (taṣarruf); Mālik distinguishes short vs long possession; al-Nasafī requires both disposition and inner conviction.
The Ḥanafī muftā bihī is that possession alone is sufficient, but the stricter conditions are recommended for caution.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The relied-upon view in the Ḥanafī school is that possession without dispute is sufficient, as the default is that the possessor is the owner unless proven otherwise.
Al-Marghīnānī in al-Hidāyah adopts this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع شيء: كان ء: أي شيء من النقود والعروض والعقار. (عيني) سوى الرقيق ذكرا كان أو أنثى الذي علم رقه، ويعبر عن نفسه، وإلا فهو كمتاع. (ط، عيني) لك أن تشهد أنه له أي إذا رأيت شيئاً في يد شخص جاز لك أن تشهد أن ذلك الشيء لمن في يده؛ لأن اليد بلا منازع أقصى ما يستدل به على الملك؛ إذ هي مرجع الدلالة في الأسباب كلها، فإن الإنسان إذا عاين البيع لا يعلم ملك المشتري إلا بملك البائع، وملك البائع لا يعلم إلا باليد وأقصى ما يستدل به كاف في الشهادة، فإنها إذا لم تجز بحكم اليد انسد بابها، وهو مفتوح بالإجماع، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه يشترط ذلك أن يقع في قلبه أن الشيء ملك لذي اليد؛ ليحصل له نوع علم أو غلبة ظن. ولهذا قيل: لو رأى درة ثمينة في يد كناس أو كتاباً في يد جاهل وليس في آبائه من هو أهل لذلك، لا يسعه أن يشهد له، وشرط "الخصاف" التصرف مع اليد، وبه قال الشافعي وأحمد، قيل: هو المختار، وعن مالك: لا تقبل في مدة يسيرة وتقبل في طويلة كعشر سنين، وشرط النسفي التصرف مع اليد وأن يقع في قلبه أنه له. ثم المسألة على أربعة أوجه الأول: أن يعاين المالك بأن عرفه باسمه ونسبه ووجهه وعرف الملك بحدوده، ورآه في يده بلا منازعة أحد، ثم رآه في يد غيره فجاء الأول وادعى الملك وسعه أن يشهد للأول بالملك بناء على يده، والثاني: أن يعاين الملك بحدوده، وينسب إلى فلان ابن فلان ولم يعرفه بوجهه ونسبه، ثم جاء الذي نسب إليه لملك، = وإن فسر للقاضي أنه يشهد بالتسامع أو بمعاينة اليد لا تقبل. ومن شهد أنه حضر أي الشاهد في موضع يجوز بالتسامع هذه الشهادة وهو الصحيح دفن فلان، أو صلّى على جنازته فهو معاينة حتى لو فسر للقاضي قبل. أي جنازة فلان أي الشاهد ذلك يسعه أن وادعى ملكية هذا المحدود على شخص حل له أن يشهد استحساناً؛ لأن المالك يصير معلوماً بالتسامع، والملك بالمعاينة، ولو لم تسمع مثل هذه لضاعت حقوق الناس؛ والثالث: أن لا يعاينهما جميعاً، ولكن سمع من الناس أنهم قالوا: إن لفلان بن فلان ضيعة في بلدة كذا، حدودها كذا، وهو لا يعرف تلك الضيعة، ولم يعاين يده عليها، لا يحل له أن يشهد له بالملك؛ لجهالة المشهود به والمشهود له، والرابع: أن يعاين المالك دون الملك، بأن عرف الرجل معرفة تامة وسمع أن له في قرية كذا ضيعة وهو لا يعرف تلك الضيعة بعينها، لا يشهد؛ لأنه لم يحصل العلم بالمحدود، والمشهود به والعلم به شرط للشهادة. وقوله: "سوى الرقيق" يعني لا يجوز له أن يشهد في الرقيق إذا رآه في يد رجل أن الرقيق ملكه؛ لأن للرقيق يداً على نفسه، حتى إذا ادعى أنه الأصل كان القول قوله، ولا يمكن أن يعتبر فيه التصرف، وهو الاستخدام؛ لأن الحر يستخدم أيضاً طائعا كالعبد، وفي "الكافي" عن أبي يوسف ومحمد أنه يجوز له أن يشهد في الرقيق إذا رآه في يده، وفي "الهداية": جعل ذلك عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً لكن فيه قيدان آخران لم يذكرهما الشيخ لله، الأول: أن لا يكون الرقيق صغيراً؛ لأن الصغير الذي لا يعبر عن نفسه يكون في يد غيره؛ إذ لا يد له على نفسه فصار كسائر الأموال، فلو كان صغيراً يجوز له أن يشهد لمن هو في يده أنه ملكه، والثاني: أن لا يعرف رقه؛ لأنه إذا عرف رقه جازت الشهادة. [ رمز الحقائق: ١٤٤/٢] والحاصل أن مصرف الاستثناء إذا كان الرقيق كبيراً يعبر نفسه؛ لأن له يدا على نفسه فليس اليد في حقه دليل الملك (عيني، فتح) عن
With something: meaning anything of cash, commodities, or real estate. (Ayni) Except slaves, male or female, whose servitude is known and who can speak for themselves; otherwise, it is like property. (T, Ayni) You may testify that it is his: i.e., if you see something in a person's hand, it is permissible for you to testify that that thing belongs to the one in whose hand it is, because possession without dispute is the utmost that can be used to infer ownership; indeed, it is the basis of evidence in all causes. For if a person witnesses a sale, he does not know the buyer's ownership except through the seller's ownership, and the seller's ownership is not known except through possession. And the utmost that can be used is sufficient for testimony; for if it were not permitted by virtue of possession, its door would be closed, yet it is open by consensus. And from Abu Yusuf: he stipulates that the witness should feel in his heart that the thing belongs to the possessor, so that he obtains some knowledge or strong assumption. Hence it was said: if he sees a precious pearl in the hand of a sweeper, or a book in the hand of an ignorant person and there is no one among his forefathers who is worthy of that, he may not testify for him. Al-Khassaf stipulated disposition (tasarruf) along with possession, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said the same; it is said this is the chosen view. From Malik: it is not accepted in a short period but is accepted in a long period, like ten years. Al-Nasafi stipulated disposition along with possession and that he feels in his heart that it is his. Then the matter is of four aspects: First: that he witnesses the owner by knowing him by name, lineage, and face, and knows the property by its boundaries, and sees it in his hand without anyone contesting, then sees it in another's hand, and the first comes and claims ownership, he may testify for the first based on his possession. Second: that he witnesses the property by its boundaries and attributes it to so-and-so, son of so-and-so, without knowing his face and lineage, then the one to whom it is attributed comes... And if he interprets for the judge that he testifies by hearsay or by seeing possession, it is not accepted. And he who testifies that he attended (the witness) in a place where hearsay is permissible, this testimony is correct: 'He buried so-and-so,' or 'He prayed over his funeral,' then it is direct, even if he interprets for the judge, it is accepted. Meaning 'the funeral of so-and-so', meaning the witness may do that. And he claimed ownership of this bounded property over someone, it is permissible for him to testify by istihsan, because the owner becomes known by hearsay and the property by witness; and if such a case were not heard, people's rights would be lost. Third: that he does not witness both, but hears from people that so-and-so, son of so-and-so, has an estate in such a town with such boundaries, and he does not know that estate nor has he seen possession of it, it is not permissible for him to testify to ownership due to ignorance of the subject and the object. Fourth: that he witnesses the owner but not the property, such that he knows the man thoroughly and hears that he has an estate in such a town, but he does not know that particular estate, he does not testify because he has not obtained knowledge of the bounded property, and knowledge is a condition for testimony. And His statement: 'except slaves' means it is not permissible for him to testify regarding a slave if he sees him in a man's hand that the slave is his property, because the slave has a hand over himself, so that if he claims that he is free, his word is taken. And disposition, i.e., utilizing him, cannot be considered because a free person may also be utilized willingly like a slave. In al-Kafi, from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is permissible for him to testify regarding a slave if he sees him in his hand. In al-Hidayah, it is attributed to Abu Hanifa as well, but with two additional conditions not mentioned by the author (may Allah have mercy on him): first, that the slave is not a minor, because a minor who cannot speak for himself is in the hand of another; he has no hand over himself, so he is like other property; if he is a minor, it is permissible to testify that he belongs to the one in whose hand he is. Second, that he does not know his servitude; if he knows his servitude, testimony is permitted. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/144] The conclusion: the meaning of the exception is if the slave is an adult who can speak for himself, because he has a hand over himself, so possession is not evidence of ownership in his case. (Ayni, Fath) 'an
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage deals with testimony based on possession (yad). The general rule is that seeing property in someone's hand without dispute is sufficient to testify that it belongs to him, because possession is the primary indicator of ownership. The commentary discusses conditions: Abu Yusuf adds that the witness must be inwardly convinced; al-Khassaf and al-Nasafi require active disposition along with possession. The four aspects (wujuh) clarify scenarios: (1) when the witness sees both owner and property, (2) when he sees the property but not the owner (allowed by istihsan because the owner becomes known by hearsay), (3) when he sees neither (not allowed), (4) when he sees the owner but not the property (not allowed). The exception for slaves is crucial: an adult slave has a hand over himself, so possession does not indicate ownership; however, a minor slave or one whose servitude is known can be testified for. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn differ on whether testimony by possession for slaves is allowed at all; the relied-upon view is that it is allowed only for minors or when servitude is known.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Possession: physical control or holding of property.
تصرف (taṣarruf): Disposition: active exercise of ownership rights (e.g., selling, using).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum evidence required to testify that property belongs to its possessor?
A) Possession without dispute (yad bila munāziʿ)
B) Possession plus disposition (tasarruf)
C) Possession for at least ten years
D) Possession plus inner conviction

Key Takeaway
Possession without dispute is sufficient for testimony of ownership, but the witness should exercise caution and ideally have inner conviction.

The Four Cases of Testimony by Possession and the Exception for Slaves
Detailed scenarios for testimony by possession and the slave exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four scenarios (wujuh) for testifying based on possession and explain why adult slaves are excepted from the general rule.

Core Idea
Testimony by possession is not absolute; it depends on whether the witness saw the owner, the property, both, or neither. Adult slaves are excluded because they have their own hand.

This lesson details the four specific scenarios (al-wujuh al-arbaʿa) for testimony based on possession, as outlined by the Hanafi scholars. It also explains the special case of slaves, where possession alone is not evidence of ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
List the four combinations of seeing owner and property: (1) see both owner and property, (2) see property only, (3) see neither, (4) see owner only.
2
Analyse each case
For each, determine whether testimony is allowed and why. Case 1: allowed. Case 2: allowed by istihsan. Cases 3 and 4: not allowed due to ignorance.
Case 2 is allowed because without it people's rights would be lost.
3
Note the exception for adult slaves
An adult slave has a hand over himself, so possession does not indicate ownership. A minor slave or one whose servitude is known can be testified for.
The text states: 'لأن للرقيق يداً على نفسه'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa permits testimony for a minor slave or when servitude is known. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad permit it based on possession alone for any slave.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view with the two conditions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that testimony for a slave is allowed only if the slave is a minor or his servitude is known.
Al-Hidayah adopts Abu Hanifa's view.

ابن فلان ولم يعرفه بوجهه ونسبه، ثم جاء الذي نسب إليه لملك، = وإن فسر للقاضي أنه يشهد بالتسامع أو بمعاينة اليد لا تقبل. ومن شهد أنه حضر أي الشاهد في موضع يجوز بالتسامع هذه الشهادة وهو الصحيح دفن فلان، أو صلّى على جنازته فهو معاينة حتى لو فسر للقاضي قبل. أي جنازة فلان أي الشاهد ذلك يسعه أن وادعى ملكية هذا المحدود على شخص حل له أن يشهد استحساناً؛ لأن المالك يصير معلوماً بالتسامع، والملك بالمعاينة، ولو لم تسمع مثل هذه لضاعت حقوق الناس؛ والثالث: أن لا يعاينهما جميعاً، ولكن سمع من الناس أنهم قالوا: إن لفلان بن فلان ضيعة في بلدة كذا، حدودها كذا، وهو لا يعرف تلك الضيعة، ولم يعاين يده عليها، لا يحل بالمحدود، والمشهود به والعلم به شرط للشهادة. وقوله: "سوى الرقيق" يعني لا يجوز له أن يشهد في الرقيق إذا رآه في يد رجل أن الرقيق ملكه؛ لأن للرقيق يداً على نفسه، حتى إذا ادعى أنه الأصل كان القول قوله، ولا يمكن أن يعتبر فيه التصرف، وهو الاستخدام؛ لأن الحر يستخدم أيضاً طائعا كالعبد، وفي "الكافي" عن أبي يوسف ومحمد أنه يجوز له أن يشهد في الرقيق إذا رآه في يده، وفي "الهداية": جعل ذلك عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً لكن فيه قيدان آخران لم يذكرهما الشيخ لله، الأول: أن لا يكون الرقيق صغيراً؛ لأن الصغير الذي لا يعبر عن نفسه يكون في يد غيره؛ إذ لا يد له على نفسه فصار كسائر الأموال، فلو كان صغيراً يجوز له أن يشهد لمن [ رمز الحقائق: ١٤٤/٢] والحاصل أن مصرف الاستثناء إذا كان الرقيق كبيراً يعبر نفسه؛ لأن له يدا على نفسه فليس اليد في حقه دليل الملك (عيني، فتح) عن
With something: meaning anything of cash, commodities, or real estate. (Ayni) Except slaves, male or female, whose servitude is known and who can speak for themselves; otherwise, it is like property. (T, Ayni) You may testify that it is his: i.e., if you see something in a person's hand, it is permissible for you to testify that that thing belongs to the one in whose hand it is, because possession without dispute is the utmost that can be used to infer ownership; indeed, it is the basis of evidence in all causes. For if a person witnesses a sale, he does not know the buyer's ownership except through the seller's ownership, and the seller's ownership is not known except through possession. And the utmost that can be used is sufficient for testimony; for if it were not permitted by virtue of possession, its door would be closed, yet it is open by consensus. And from Abu Yusuf: he stipulates that the witness should feel in his heart that the thing belongs to the possessor, so that he obtains some knowledge or strong assumption. Hence it was said: if he sees a precious pearl in the hand of a sweeper, or a book in the hand of an ignorant person and there is no one among his forefathers who is worthy of that, he may not testify for him. Al-Khassaf stipulated disposition (tasarruf) along with possession, and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said the same; it is said this is the chosen view. From Malik: it is not accepted in a short period but is accepted in a long period, like ten years. Al-Nasafi stipulated disposition along with possession and that he feels in his heart that it is his. Then the matter is of four aspects: First: that he witnesses the owner by knowing him by name, lineage, and face, and knows the property by its boundaries, and sees it in his hand without anyone contesting, then sees it in another's hand, and the first comes and claims ownership, he may testify for the first based on his possession. Second: that he witnesses the property by its boundaries and attributes it to so-and-so, son of so-and-so, without knowing his face and lineage, then the one to whom it is attributed comes... And if he interprets for the judge that he testifies by hearsay or by seeing possession, it is not accepted. And he who testifies that he attended (the witness) in a place where hearsay is permissible, this testimony is correct: 'He buried so-and-so,' or 'He prayed over his funeral,' then it is direct, even if he interprets for the judge, it is accepted. Meaning 'the funeral of so-and-so', meaning the witness may do that. And he claimed ownership of this bounded property over someone, it is permissible for him to testify by istihsan, because the owner becomes known by hearsay and the property by witness; and if such a case were not heard, people's rights would be lost. Third: that he does not witness both, but hears from people that so-and-so, son of so-and-so, has an estate in such a town with such boundaries, and he does not know that estate nor has he seen possession of it, it is not permissible for him to testify to ownership due to ignorance of the subject and the object. Fourth: that he witnesses the owner but not the property, such that he knows the man thoroughly and hears that he has an estate in such a town, but he does not know that particular estate, he does not testify because he has not obtained knowledge of the bounded property, and knowledge is a condition for testimony. And His statement: 'except slaves' means it is not permissible for him to testify regarding a slave if he sees him in a man's hand that the slave is his property, because the slave has a hand over himself, so that if he claims that he is free, his word is taken. And disposition, i.e., utilizing him, cannot be considered because a free person may also be utilized willingly like a slave. In al-Kafi, from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is permissible for him to testify regarding a slave if he sees him in his hand. In al-Hidayah, it is attributed to Abu Hanifa as well, but with two additional conditions not mentioned by the author (may Allah have mercy on him): first, that the slave is not a minor, because a minor who cannot speak for himself is in the hand of another; he has no hand over himself, so he is like other property; if he is a minor, it is permissible to testify that he belongs to the one in whose hand he is. Second, that he does not know his servitude; if he knows his servitude, testimony is permitted. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/144] The conclusion: the meaning of the exception is if the slave is an adult who can speak for himself, because he has a hand over himself, so possession is not evidence of ownership in his case. (Ayni, Fath) 'an
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage deals with testimony based on possession (yad). The general rule is that seeing property in someone's hand without dispute is sufficient to testify that it belongs to him, because possession is the primary indicator of ownership. The commentary discusses conditions: Abu Yusuf adds that the witness must be inwardly convinced; al-Khassaf and al-Nasafi require active disposition along with possession. The four aspects (wujuh) clarify scenarios: (1) when the witness sees both owner and property, (2) when he sees the property but not the owner (allowed by istihsan because the owner becomes known by hearsay), (3) when he sees neither (not allowed), (4) when he sees the owner but not the property (not allowed). The exception for slaves is crucial: an adult slave has a hand over himself, so possession does not indicate ownership; however, a minor slave or one whose servitude is known can be testified for. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn differ on whether testimony by possession for slaves is allowed at all; the relied-upon view is that it is allowed only for minors or when servitude is known.

Key Terms
رقيق (raqīq): Slave: a person owned as property.
يد (yad): Possession: physical control or holding of property.
