(عيني)] قيد بالظهور؛ لأنه لو كتمه تقبل شهادته، ولو قال: "أو يظهر سب "مسلم" لكان أولى؛ لأن العدالة تسقط مسلم، وإن لم يكن من السلف؛ لأن السب يدل على قلة المروءة وقصور العقل، وعن أبي يوسف: لا أقبل شهادة من سب الصحابة، وأقبلها ممن تبرأ منهم؛ لأنهم يعتقدون ديناً، وإن كان على باطل، فلم يظهر فسقه، بخلاف الساب. (عيني، فتح
Chapter of whose testimony is accepted. Or he sings for people, or commits what necessitates a hadd punishment, or enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper, or consumes usury... because he commits a major sin against himself. Do you not see that people construct dovecotes for doves without reproach, except when they leave the house, they bring doves of others and they breed in his house, and he eats and sells from them and does not distinguish them from his own doves, so it becomes consuming the forbidden, thus his uprightness falls by that. And in some copies: 'or plays the tanbur' which is more appropriate to his saying 'or sings'. And in al-'Inaya: it is dispensed with by his saying 'sings for people', for singing is more general, whether with a musical instrument or not. (Ayni, Fath, Inaya) And he sings for people: [This is general encompassing men and women, so no repetition. (Ayni)] because it gathers people for amusement and play, so his testimony is not accepted. And the singer is one who makes people hear his singing; because if it is for his own listening to ward off loneliness without others hearing, then there is no harm, and his uprightness does not fall in the correct view. And if he recites poetry containing admonition and wisdom, it is permissible by consensus. And if it contains mention of a specific woman, if she is dead or an unspecified woman, then no harm; if she is specific and alive, it is disliked. Some mashayikh permitted singing at a wedding, do you not see that there is no harm in beating the duff therein to announce the marriage? And some said: if he sings to benefit from refining poetry and become eloquent in tongue, there is no harm. And some disliked it absolutely, some permitted it absolutely. The apparent meaning from the author's words is the non-permissibility of singing absolutely. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/147] Or commits what necessitates hadd, like zina, theft, sodomy, and other major sins; because whoever commits them does not care about lying. And his words indicate that what requires hadd is a major sin. They differed on them: the people of Hijaz and hadith say they are the seven mentioned in the famous hadith: shirk with Allah, fleeing from battle, disobedience to parents, killing a soul, slandering a believer, zina, and drinking wine. Some added consuming usury and consuming orphan's wealth unlawfully. And it is said: what is proven forbidden by a definitive proof is a major sin. And some said: what has a hadd or killing is a major sin. And some said: everything that one persists upon is a major sin, and what one seeks forgiveness for is a minor sin. The most appropriate is what the theologians mentioned: every sin above which is a sin and below which is a sin, so relative to what is above it is minor, and relative to what is below it is major. The most correct is what is transmitted from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that he said: what is ugly among Muslims, involving violation of the sanctity of Allah and religion, is among the major sins. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/148] Without a waist-wrapper: because he commits the forbidden, since revealing the 'awrah is forbidden. (Ayni) Or consumes usury because it is a major sin, whether notorious or not. (T) He takes the excess amount, because the excess is meant in the verse: 'and Allah has forbidden usury' (al-Baqara 2:275). And he used 'consumes' following the verse, because it is the greatest benefit of wealth, and because usury is common in foodstuffs. Testimony of the consumer of usury is not accepted because it is a major sin. In al-Asl, it is conditioned that he be notorious for it, by persistence, because it is impossible to guard against invalid contracts which are usury, unlike consuming orphan's wealth where persistence is not required because guarding against it is possible. The gist is that fisq itself prevents acceptance of testimony except that the judge does not suspect until after its appearance, so all are equal. (Ayni, Fath) Or gambles with backgammon and chess, or misses prayer because of them, or urinates or eats on the road, or displays reviling of the salaf... (the commentary continues on backgammon and chess, urinating/eating on road, and reviling the salaf) ...
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on testimony, listing factors that disqualify a witness. The author presents each disqualifier and the commentary expands with proofs and madhhab positions. Singing to gather people for amusement is a disqualifier; singing alone or for admonition is acceptable. Committing major sins (kaba'ir) as defined by various scholars disqualifies; the relied-upon definition is that which is ugly and violates sanctity. Entering a bathhouse without a waist-wrapper is fisq due to exposing 'awrah. Consuming usury (riba) is a major sin; persistence is required for disqualification unless notorious. Gambling with backgammon (nard) disqualifies immediately per hadith, while chess (shatranj) only disqualifies if combined with gambling, missing prayer, or frequent false oaths. Acts that violate muru'a (chivalry), like urinating/eating in public, disqualify if persistent. Reviling the salaf (pious predecessors) disqualifies; merely disassociating (tabarru') does not, per Abu Yusuf. The Hanafi position is consistently that these actions indicate lack of 'adala (integrity).

Key Terms
النرد (al-nard): Backgammon; playing it is fisq and disqualifies testimony immediately.
الشطرنج (al-shatranj): Chess; only disqualifies if accompanied by gambling, missing prayer, or frequent false oaths.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following statements is correct about consuming usury (riba)?
A) It never disqualfies testimony because it is a financial transaction
B) It is a major sin that disqualfies testimony, but the judge needs evidence of persistence
C) Only persistent consumption disqualfies, and a single instance does not
D) It disqualfies only if combined with gambling

Key Takeaway
Backgammon disqualfies immediately; chess disqualfies only with additional violations; consuming usury is a major sin that disqualfies once known.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
7 min
Acts Against Muru'ah and Reviling the Salaf
Acts against muru'ah and reviling salaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify acts that violate muru'ah (public decency) and explain how reviling the salaf disqualfies a witness according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Acts that violate public decency, even if not haram, can disqualfy if done persistently; reviling the salaf is fisq and disqualfies, but mere disassociation is not.

This lesson covers two additional disqualifiers: acts that violate muru'ah (like urinating or eating in public, wrestling in the mosque, excessive joking, etc.) and reviling the salaf (pious predecessors). The text explains that these actions indicate a lack of shame or religious commitment, which undermines 'adala. Reviling the salaf is fisq, but Abu Yusuf distinguishes between reviling and disassociating.

Guided Path
1
Identify acts that violate muru'ah
The text lists: urinating or eating on the road, stretching legs before people, wrestling children in the mosque, stealing a morsel, excessive joking leading to contempt, keeping bad company, and being a buffoon.
These acts are not necessarily haram but reflect lack of decency.
2
Understand the condition of persistence
The commentary emphasizes that these acts only disqualfy if done persistently (idman). A single occurrence may not destroy 'adala.
This is a safeguard against over-strictness.
3
Analyze reviling the salaf
Reviling (sabb) of the salaf (companions, tabi'un, and major scholars like Abu Hanifa) is fisq and disqualfies. The condition 'displaying' (izhar) means if hidden, testimony is accepted.
Abu Yusuf: reviling disqualfies, but disassociating (tabarra) does not because it is a belief issue not fisq.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a witness who occasionally jokes excessively but repents. Or one who speaks ill of the Sahaba in private. Determine acceptance based on persistence and publicity.
Practice distinguishing public from private, and persistent from occasional.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner

Acceptable Testimonies Despite Relations and for People of Innovation
Listing acceptable testimonies despite relations and for ahl al-hawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the relatives and groups for which testimony is accepted in Hanafi fiqh, and explain the rationale of lack of suspicion (tuhma).

Core Idea
Testimony for specific relatives and ahl al-hawa is accepted because no suspicion of bias exists.

The Hanafi school recognizes that familial relations can create suspicion of bias in testimony, but not in all cases. This passage from al-Kanz lists the relatives for whom testimony is accepted despite the relationship, and extends this to people of innovation (ahl al-hawa). The key principle is 'lack of suspicion' (adam al-tuhma).

Guided Path
1
Identify the list
Read the passage and note all the relatives and groups mentioned: brother, uncle, parents through breastfeeding, mother-in-law, stepdaughter, son-in-law, daughter-in-law, father, and people of innovation.
The list includes both blood relatives (e.g., brother) and in-laws.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is 'lack of suspicion' (adam al-tuhma). Consider why these specific relations do not create a suspicion of bias, unlike some other relations.
Hanafis hold that distinct financial interests or lack of close household ties remove suspicion.
3
Note the consensus and the Hanafi position on ahl al-hawa
The passage states this ruling is by consensus. For ahl al-hawa, Hanafis accept their testimony because they do not consider themselves sinful, so their fisq is not manifest.
Other schools like Shafi'i differ on ahl al-hawa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقبل لأخيه وعمه وأبويه رضاعاً وأم امرأته وبنتها ك ف د وزوج بنته وامرأة ابنه وأبيه وأهل الهوى أي ولأجل امرأة ابنه لعدم التهمة وهذا بالإجماع أي و
And testimony is accepted for his brother, his uncle, his parents through breastfeeding, the mother of his wife and his daughter, and the husband of his daughter, and the wife of his son, and his father, and people of desire (innovation). That is, on behalf of his son's wife, due to lack of suspicion, and this is by consensus.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the same chapter, listing persons for whom testimony is acceptable despite familial relations. The text states that one may testify for one's brother, uncle, parents by breastfeeding, mother-in-law, stepdaughter, son-in-law, daughter-in-law, father, and also for 'ahl al-hawa' (people of innovation). The reason given is lack of suspicion (tuhma) because ownerships are distinct. The commentary (not fully shown in the OCR) explains that this is by consensus. The acceptance for ahl al-hawa is surprising because they are considered fasiq in belief, but their testimony is accepted because they do not consider themselves sinful, so their fisq is not manifest. The Hanafi position is that testimony of ahl al-hawa is accepted as long as they do not engage in lying or other disqualifying acts.

Key Terms
الرضاع (al-rida'): Breastfeeding; the parents through breastfeeding are considered mahram and testimony for them is accepted.
أهل الهوى (ahl al-hawa): People of innovation; those who follow their desires and oppose the Sunnah without legal or rational evidence.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of bias that would affect testimony; it is absent here due to distinct ownerships.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school accept testimony of ahl al-hawa (people of innovation) despite their deviant beliefs?
A) Because they are considered just in worldly matters
B) Because they do not consider themselves sinful, so their fisq is not manifest
C) Because all Muslims are equal in testimony
D) Only if they repent

Key Takeaway
Testimony for specific relatives and ahl al-hawa is accepted in Hanafi fiqh due to the principle of lack of suspicion (adam al-tuhma).

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony of Gamblers: Nard and Chess in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on testimony of gamblers with nard and chess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a nard player and a chess player, explain why they differ, and apply the distinction to similar cases.

Core Idea
Nard alone disqualifies a witness; chess only disqualifies with added fisq.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a critical issue in the chapter on testimony: the legal status of a witness who plays nard (backgammon) or chess. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between the two games, rooted in a specific hadith and the scope of ijtihad. Understanding this distinction is essential for a judge evaluating witness reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two games and their initial rulings
Note that for nard, testimony is rejected outright. For chess, it is accepted unless specific conditions exist.
The ruling for nard is absolute; chess is conditional.
2
Examine the dalil for nard
The hadith 'Cursed is the one who plays nard' explicitly declares the player cursed, indicating major sin (fisq). A fasiq is not a reliable witness.
The curse (la'n) is a strong textual indication.
3
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning for chess
Chess is not explicitly condemned; there is room for ijtihad. Hence, playing chess alone is not fisq. It only becomes fisq when combined with gambling, missing prayer, or frequent false oaths.
This is the key distinction.
4
Map the inter-madhhab dispute
Malik and al-Shafi'i consider chess permissible, so they accept testimony unconditionally. The Hanafi position is more cautious, rejecting testimony only when conditions of fisq are attached.
The practical consequence differs between courts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو يقامر بالنرد والشطرنج، أو تفوته الصلاة بسببهما. من المقامرة وهي التراهن في اللعب مأخوذ من القمر؛ لأن ماله يزداد إذا غلب وينقص إذا غلب كالقمر يزيد وينقص والشطرنج بكسر أوله والفتح، والسين المهملة لغة فيه. (عيني، فتح) أو تفوته الصلاة أي النرد والشطرنج؛ لأن كل ذلك فسق فلا تقبل الشهادة، وكذا إذا كان يكثر عليهما الحلف كاذباً، وقالوا: في النرد ترد شهادته بمجرد اللعب فيه من غير اشتراط القمار ولا غيره؛ لأن نفس اللعب فيه فسق، وقال عليه السلام: "ملعون من يلعب بالنرد"، ومن يكون ملعوناً لم يكن عدلاً، بخلاف الشطرنج؛ لأن للاجتهاد فيه مساغاً، فإن مالكا والشافعي يقولان بحل لعب الشطرنج، فلا ترد شهادته ما لم ينضم إليه أحد وهي: القمار وفوت الصلاة وكثرة الحلف وزاد بعضهم عليها ثلاثة آخر وهي: اللعب به على الطريق وأن يذكر عليه فسقا وأن يداوم عليه. (عيني، فتح)
Or he gambles with nard and chess, or the prayer is missed due to them. (Explanation of gambling: It is wagering in play, derived from 'qamar' because his wealth increases if he wins and decreases if he loses, like the moon waxes and wanes. Chess, with kasra on the first letter and fatha, and with the unpointed sin, is a variant language. ( al-'Ayni, al-Fath ) Or the prayer is missed, meaning due to nard and chess, because all that is fisq so his testimony is not accepted. Likewise if he frequently lies when swearing by them. They said: Regarding nard, his testimony is rejected merely by playing it, without stipulating gambling or anything else, because playing it itself is fisq. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Cursed is the one who plays nard.' And one who is cursed cannot be upright. Contrary to chess, because there is room for ijtihad concerning it. Verily Malik and al-Shafi'i say playing chess is permissible, so his testimony is not rejected unless one of the following is attached to it: gambling, missing prayer, or frequent swearing. And some added three more: playing it on the road, mentioning fisq upon it, and persisting in it.)
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the testimony of a person who gambles with nard (backgammon) or shatranj (chess). The author explains that gambling (qimar) is wagering in play, derived from the word 'qamar' (moon) because one's wealth waxes and wanes like the moon. The term 'shatranj' is explained linguistically. The key ruling: playing nard alone renders one a fasiq and his testimony is rejected, based on the hadith 'Cursed is the one who plays nard' — a cursed person cannot be an upright witness. In contrast, chess is treated differently because there is room for ijtihad; Malik and al-Shafi'i consider it permissible. Therefore, a chess player's testimony is only rejected if one of three additional conditions is present: gambling (qimar), missing prayer due to it, or frequent false oaths. Some scholars add three more: playing on the road, mentioning fisq upon it, and persisting in it. This reflects an inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafis (based on Abu Hanifa's view) consider chess playing as makruh but not automatically fisq, unlike nard.

Key Terms
النرد (al-nard): A game of dice (backgammon) played with pieces and dice, involving chance.
الشطرنج (al-shatranj): Chess, a game of strategy on a board.
المقامرة (al-muqamarah): Gambling or wagering in play, derived from qamar (moon) because wealth waxes and wanes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition is the testimony of a chess player rejected?
A) Always, because playing chess is fisq.
B) Never, because chess is halal.
C) Only if gambling, missing prayer, or frequent swearing is attached.
D) Only if he plays on the road.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between nard (automatically fisq) and chess (only fisq with additional conditions), based on the hadith cursing nard players and the scope of ijtihad for chess.
